Kolkata is a Megacity in India governed by the municipal corporation, which is of the type found in India. The city has a population of 4496694, is located at 9.0 and has a postal code of 700 xxx. Kolkata is the birthplace of Amrita Chattopadhyay, Prabhas Kumar Choudhary, Prabodh Panda, Amlan Das Gupta, Potol Kumar Gaanwala, Carmel School (located in the city), and Bela Mukherjee. The UTC offset is +05:30 and the area codes are 33. Kolkata is the location of Calcutta Boys' School, the Carmel School, and the school of Poulomi Das. It is also the death place of Prabhas Kumar Choudhary.
Koror is the capital of Palau and the home of many notable people including Ruby Joy Gabriel, Sandra Pierantozzi, David Ramarui, and Thomas Remengesau Sr. It is also the location of the Belau National Museum, the Belau Air headquarters and the Ministry of Education HQ. The city has a population of 11444 and a density of 176 per sq km. Its area code is 488 and its postal code 96940. The city is also the location for the spoken Tobian language, the Hokkons Baules Tenure, 2010 Micronesian Games, 2005 South Pacific Mini Games, T8AA-FM, Uet era Ngermeuangel, and Uet era Ongael.
Kotte, Sri Lanka is home to the Socialist Equality Party. St Thomas' College, Kotte and Ananda Balika Vidyalaya can also be found in the city. Milton Mallawarachchi, P D Premasiri and Herbert M Seneviratne were all born in the city. Ananda Sastralaya, Kotte was the location of the Ming-Kotte War.
Kuala Lumpur is a federal territory of Malaysia and was founded on February 1, 1972. Its governing body is the Kuala Lumpur City Hall which has a local government. Its type of government is a federal territory, it is also the capital of Malaysia and it is also the birth place of Prabakaran Parameswaran, Rolf W. Schnyder, Carrie Lee Sze Kei, Puvaneswaran Ramasamy and Sanusi Junid. Kuala Lumpur has the UTC offset of +8, its area code is 50000 to 60000, and its population total is 1,982,112. Its population density is 2708.0, its area is 243.0, its elevation is 63.0, and its current flag is called Maju Dan Sejahtera. Kuala Lumpur was bombed in 1945 and one of the battles that were fought there was the Battle of Kuala Lumpur. Some of the attractions there are Carcosa Seri Negara and Prasarana Malaysia.
Kuwait City, Kuwait is the capital and home to the government in exile. The city hosts the AFC cup finals 2009 and 2010 and the Asian airgun championships in 2011. The city also hosted the Conference Board. It is also the location of the city of Roony Bardghji, Samer Al Marta, Sanjeeda Sheikh, Jovan Šarčević, Mathunny Mathews, Ghanam Al-Jumhur, Bashar al-Shatti, Yousif Nizar Saleh and Ammar Al-Tamimi. Kuwait City is the type of capital city in Kuwait and its people observe UTC+3. The city is also the location of the Kuwait Army's garrison, the Ministry of Information's headquarters, the Ministry of Commerce and Industry's headquarters, and the grounds of Al-Sulaibikhat SC.
La Paz, with an area of 472.0 (square kilometres), is a city in the Republic of Alto Peru, with a population of 766,468. Founded on 20 October 1548, La Paz has a total area of 3240000000.0, a population density of 1861.2440654697148, and an elevation of 3639.9216. La Paz has a type of executive government, and its time zone is UTC - 4. The country is the capital of Bolivia, and its postal code ranges from 0201-0220. The current motto is "The dissenters in harmony gathered together in peace and love, and a town of peace they founded, for perpetual memory." La Paz is the birthplace of Carlos Iturralde Ballivián, Carlos Mendoza, Carlos Mesa, and Julia Elena Fortún. It is also the place of residence of Octavia. La Paz is the site of the Basilica of San Francisco, the Peasant Research and Promotion Center, the Estadio Hernando Siles, the 2012-2013 Club Bolivar season, the ground of the Club Deportivo Litoral (La Paz), the newspaper Cambio, and the newspaper Bolivia. It is also the location of the Upper Peru capital, the University of Our Lady of La Paz, and the Bolivian Catholic University of San Pablo. La Paz is the site of the Cambio newspaper's headquarters and the Página Siete newspaper's headquarters. It is the deathplace of Bartolina Sisa and Belisario Salinas.
Lahore is the city in Pakistan where the Mongol invasion of India took place in 1297-1298 and also the site of the Battle of Lahore (1752). It is a local government city in Punjab with a population of 11126285 and a land area of 1772.0. Its UTC offset is +5 and has a postal code of 54000. It is also home to the Punjab Educational Endowment Fund, the Punjab Forensic Science Agency and the site of the Amna Mufti, Ammar Aziz, Pran Chopra, Qari Ghulam Rasool and Qasim Mahmood birthplaces. 042 is the area code for Lahore and it has a time zone of Pakistan Standard Time.
Gabon's capital city is Libreville, which is the location of the country's parliament, the airport, several sports grounds and stadiums, and the main city for the Gabonese Air Force, Navy, and Air Force. Libreville is also the birthplace of many notable Gabonese people including Rodrigue Moundounga, Romaric Rogombé, Rose Christiane Raponda, Léon-Mébiame, Paul-Marie Yembit, and Joseph Novales. Libreville is also where the 2019 Gabonese coup d'état attempt took place, and where Air Trans Africa targeted Libreville International Airport. Libreville is also home to many other notable sites such as the Prytanée militaire de Libreville, the 2012 Africa Cup of Nations Final, the Central African Games of 1976, the Léon-Mba International airport, and the grounds of Okoume FC, Zalang COC, and Region Air. Sky Gabon and Nouvelle Air Affaires Gabon both have their headquarters in the city, and Christelle Avomo and Wilfried Bingangoye have both made the city their home. Libreville is the closest city to the Atlantic Ocean and is the location of the song Mario was recorded in.
The capital city of Malawi is Lilongwe where the Bingu National Stadium is located. The city has a population of 989,318, with a total area of 727.79 square kilometers, and its UTC offset is +2. EPAC United FC, Democratic Progressive Party (Malawi), Media Institute of Southern Africa Malawi, and Malawi Airlines headquarters are also located in Lilongwe. The city is the largest city in the country.
Lima is the capital city of Peru and is located at the coast in the western Peru. Lima was founded by Francisco Pizarro on January 18, 1535 and has a total area of 2672.3 square kilometres. The city has 10,882,757 people living in it and has the UTC offset of -5. Ljubljana is the capital city of Slovenia and its region is served by Ljubljana Passenger Transport. It is located at 295.0 meters and 163.8 square kilometers. Ljubljana was founded on 6-12-1461 and its population and area total are 295,504 and 23,340,000,000 square kilometers respectively. The city is home to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of Slovenia and the Cankar Centre. It is the birthplace of, Anton Stres, Bele Vrane, Christian Gostečnik, Primož Gliha, Primož Jakopin, Primož Kozak, Roža Piščanec, and Niet. The capital city of Togo, and the country's largest city, is Lomé. It has a total area of 99.14 km² and a population of 837,437 (the population of the metropolitan area is 28,000,000,000 and the population density is 5608.0 per square kilometer). Lomé is at an elevation of 10 meters above sea level. It is home to a number of landmarks and sites, such as the University of Science and Technology of Togo, the CIFAD campus, and the Sacred Heart Cathedral. It is also where several notable Togolese were born, including Samson Johnson, Massamasso Tchangai, and Prince Segbefia. The city is the site of the Lomé-Tokoin International Airport, the Togoland capital, and is also the location of the Democratic Convention of African Peoples, the Union of Forces for Change, and the West African Development Bank. 1963, 1967, and 1986 were the sites of coup attempts in the city. 1967 Togolese Coup, 1986 Togolese coup, CIFAD, CO Model de Lomé, Democratic Convention of African Peoples, Edmond Apeti Kaolo, Fambaré Ouattara Natchaba, Hotel 2 Fevrier Lomé, King Mensah, Lomé, Massamasso Tchangai, Prince Segbefia, Samson Johnson, Togo Telecom FC, Union of Forces for Change, University of Science and Technology of Togo, West African Development Bank.
London is the capital city of the United Kingdom and its governing body is the Mayor of London. It is 11.0 metres above sea level and covers an area of 1572.03. Its total population is 8,799,800 (metro 14257962) and has a population density of 5598.0. The time zone in London is British Summer Time and it is Greenwich Mean Time. London is the type of capital city and is governed by a deliberative assembly, directly elected mayors in England and Wales and the Cabinet Office. Callum Blue, Callum Daniel and Caleb Quaye were all born in London. Battle of Lewisham, the Battle of Britain day, Cad and the Dandy, Caffè Nero were all located there. The Despenser War was also fought there.

Luanda is the capital city of Angola and is located along the Atlantic Ocean, with a total area of 116 square kilometers and population of 2571861. The city is the home to many people including Diamondog, Banco de Poupança e Crédito, Movicel, and Miss Angola. The city has a total area of 116.0, a population of 2571861 and is the home of the Luanda Bay. Many people are Luandans or Luandense (Portuguese) and the city is home to several sports teams such as the Santos Futebol Clube de Angola and the G.D. Interclube. Luanda is also home to the National Air Force of Angola and the Angolan Army, and is also the location of the headquarters of the Humanist Party of Angola, the Ministry of Science and Technology (Angola) and the rallying point for the Volkswagen Polo Mk4 assembly line. Carlinhos, Capita, Carlos Almeida, Paulão and David Zé were all born in Luanda, as well as Adolfo Luxúria Canibal. It was the capital of the United Provinces of British India and the Oudh state. Einstein was awarded the Copley Medal, Barnard Medal for Meritorious Service to Science, and was a member of the National Academy of Sciences. Einstein married twice, first to Elsa Einstein and then to Mileva Maric. Einstein was known for Bose-Einstein statistics, the EPR paradox, and ensemble interpretation. He influenced Hendrik Lorentz and Hermann Minkowski and was influenced by Samarendra Kumar Mitra. Einstein was the author of The Meaning of Relativity and starred in the film Atomic Power. Psychologist and psychiatrist Carl Gustav Jung was born in Canton of Thurgau on July 26, 1875. His alma mater was the University of Basel and his doctoral advisor was Eugen Bleuler. He was married to Emma Jung and his spouse was Sabina Spielrein. He died on June 6, 1961 in the Canton of Zurich. He won many awards including the Royal Society of Medicine and the University of Allahabad. He was known for complexes, archetypes and analytical psychology. He was also influenced by Carl Gustav Carus, Meister Eckhart and Friedrich Nietzsche. He wrote Psychological Types, Psychology of the Unconscious, Memories, Dreams, Reflections. His doctoral student was Carl Jung and his influenced were Carl Gustav Carus, Meister Eckhart and Friedrich Nietzsche. It is worth noting that Jung's doctoral advisor was Eugen Bleuler and he was awarded the University of Allahabad and the University of Calcutta.

Charlemagne, who ruled between 768 and 0814 and was succeeded by Louis the Pious and Desiderius, was the father of Pepin of Italy, Louis the Pious, Charles the Younger and Tekla Teresa Lubienska. His parents were Pepin the Short and Bertrada of Laon. He was the commander in the Siege of Pavia (773-774), the Battle of Roncevaux Pass, and the Saxon Wars. He founded the Gymnasium Theodorianum and was the grandfather of Richbod. His own children included Rotrude and Luitgard (Frankish queen). His wives included Fastrada and Desideria of the Lombards. His own successor was Carloman I. 0768 and 0814 were the years that Charlemagne began and ended his reign.

Charles Darwin was born on the 12th of February 1809 in Shrewsbury. His spouse was Emma Darwin. He is known for the books The Voyage of the Beagle, Insectivorous Plants, Geological Observations on the Volcanic Islands and On the Origin of Species. He also won the Copley Medal, Pour le Mérite and the Royal Medal. His death place was in Downe on the 19th of April, 1882. He was influenced by Alexander von Humboldt, Charles Lyell and John Herschel. His parents were Robert Darwin and Emma Wedgwood, and his child is Horace Darwin. His wife is Henrietta Litchfield. He studied geology and natural history.
Charles John Huffam Dickens, who was born in Portsmouth on February 7th 1812, was the author of many notable works, including Oliver Twist, David Copperfield and Nicholas Nickleby. He also wrote Mrs Bardell (Pickwick Papers), The Daily News (UK), American Notes and Memoirs of Joseph Grimaldi. Dickens died on 9 June 1870 in Higham, Kent. He was married to Catherine Dickens, with whom he had several children, including Dora Annie, Edward, Francis and Walter Landor. Charles Maurice de Talleyrand-Périgord was a member of the Legitimist party and a member of the Doctrinaires. He was a politician, diplomat, and clergyman. Talleyrand-Périgord died on 17th May, 1838 in Paris. He was an independent politician. He began his career in 1952 and ended it in 2014. Mowat graduated from the University of Toronto and was married to Claire Mowat. He is known for A Whale for the Killing, Canada 98 and for his involvement with the North American Native Plant Society.
The Strait of Magellan was named after explorer Ferdinand Magellan, who was born on February 4, 1480 as Fernão de Magalhães in Sabrosa. He died on April 27, 1521 at Mactan. Magellan is famous for his round-the-world trip, his involvement in the Pacific Ocean and his involvement in the Moroccan-Portuguese conflicts where he was a commander. He was born in 1480 and died in 1521.
Fernando Henrique Cardoso was born in Rio de Janeiro on 18 June 1931 and attended the University of São Paulo. A professional Sociologist, he was married to Ruth Cardoso. He was a member of the Brazilian Democratic Movement Party and later of the Brazilian Social Democracy Party. He resided in São Paulo. He was president of the Tenure 6 of Pérsio Arida, Tenure 4 of Raul Jungmann, Tenure 3 of Renan Calheiros, Tenure 2 of Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva, Tenure 1 of Eva Alterman Blay, Tenure 1 of Franco Montoro and of Itamar Franco. He was succeeded by Celso Lafer. Cardoso was also the starring of the movie "Breaking the Taboo".
Florence Nightingale was born in Grand Duchy of Tuscany on 12 May 1820 and died in Mayfair on 13 August 1910. Her academic disciplines included sanitation and hygiene. She was the child of William Nightingale. The notable work of Davide Danti includes work related to Florence Nightingale. Nazaria Lagos is known for Florence Nightingale. The Shanti Teresa Lakra Award is the Florence Nightingale Award.
Born in London, on January 22nd, 1561, and died on April 9th, 1626, in the Kingdom of England, Francis Bacon, was married to Alice Barnham. Francis was educated at Gray's Inn and was the author of the following works: Novum Organum, The History of the Reign of King Henry the Seventh, and New Atlantis. Robert Boyle, George Campbell (minister), Giambattista Vico, and Sir Henry Hobart, 1st Baronet (Tenure 2) were all influenced by Francis Bacon.
Francisco Pizarro was born in the Crown of Castile in 1478-03-16 and died on 1541-06-26 in the Governorate of New Castile. He was married to Quispe Sisa and had a child, Francisca Pizarro Yupanqui. Francisco Pizarro founded Lima and was a commander at the Battle of Cajamarca, the Battle of Cusco and the Battle of Punta Quemada.
François Marie Adrien Maurice Mitterrand (born Jarnac on October 26th 1916) died on 8th January 1996 in Paris. He was married to Danielle Mitterrand and had many notable achievements including commanding the Mountain War in Lebanon and the Siege of Sarajevo. He was president of the Convention of Republican Institutions and the Federation of the Democratic and Socialist Left, and was succeeded by Alain Savary and Leon Martinaud-Déplat. He was a predecessor of Jacques Chirac and Lionel Jospin and was succeeded by Valéry Giscard d'Estaing and René Monory. Freddie Mercury was born in Stone Town, on the 5th of September 1946. He went to Ealing Art College and the West Thames College, and he died on the 24th of November, 1991, from bronchopneumonia, in Kensington. His real name was Farrokh Bulsara and he used the alias, Freddie Bulsara. He was a singer for Queen and a number of other bands. He performed at the band's performance at Wembley. He was also the composer of the Golden Boy, In My Defence and Super Fun Night. The songs Love Kills, Love Me Like There's No Tomorrow and Made in Heaven were performed by him. He wrote Bicycle Race and Body Language. Giorgio Moroder and Jo Burt are associated with Freddie Mercury and he performed with the Sour Milk Sea band.
Frederick Banting was a Canadian born in Alliston, on 14 November 1891. He attended the University of Toronto and died in the Dominion of Newfoundland on 21 February 1941. Banting won the Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine, the Cameron Prize in Therapeutics, and the Military Cross. He is known for his work on insulin.

The writer Gabriel Garcia Marquez was born in Aracataca, on the 6th of March 1927. He was married to Mercedes Barcha and had a son named Rodrigo. His Alma mater was the National University of Colombia. Gabriel Garcia Marquez died on the 17th of April 2014 in Mexico City. He was the author of The Autumn of the Patriarch, Love in the Time of Cholera, Chronicle of a Death Foretold, Memories of My Melancholy Whores and The Summer of Miss Forbes. El Año de la Peste was written by Gabriel Garcia Marquez as was The Widow of Montiel.
The anatomy discipline, influenced by Aristotle, Herophilos and Hippocrates, also a student of medicine, Galen was born in Bergama and also studied philosophy. Galen was also influenced by Ali ibn Ridwan.
Galileo Galilei was born in the Duchy of Florence on February 15th, 1564 as Galileo di Vincenzo Bonaiuti de' Galilei. His academic background included Maths, Engineering and Physics. Galileo is known for kinematics, analytical dynamics and observational astronomy, and is also known for his work on the celestial bodies such as the moon Callisto, Europa and Ganymede. He was influenced by Nicolaus Copernicus and John Philoponus and died on 8th January, 1642 in Arcetri. Galileo is known for discovering many celestial bodies and is the author of the book Two New Sciences, as well as Dialogo de Cecco di Ronchitti da Bruzene in perpuosito de la stella Nuova and Sidereus Nuncius. He is known to have influenced Robert Boyle.
Gao Xingjian, born in Ganzhou on the 4th of January 1940, graduated from Beijing Foreign Studies University. He is an exponent of the Chinese language and literature in Absurdism, some of his notable works include "Soul Mountain", "The Bus Stop" and "The Other Shore", all written by Gao Xingjian.
Gary Becker was born on 02/12/1930 in Pottsville, Pennsylvania, and died on 03/05/2014 in Chicago, Illinois. He graduated from Princeton University and the University of Chicago, and went on to influence many others including Edi Karni, Abel's Island's cinematographer, Peter Leeson and Milton Friedman. He was awarded the John Bates Clark Medal, National Medal of Science and the John von Neumann Award for his work in economics. Theodore Schultz also influenced him.
Geddy Lee was born on July 29th, 1953 in North York. His career began in 1968 as a solo singer in progressive rock and hard rock. Genghis Khan, who started his career in 1206, was married to Ibaqa Beki, Börte, and Möge Khatun. His children included Alakhai Bekhi, Ögedei Khan, and Tolui. Ögedei Khan succeeded Genghis Khan, as did Tolui. Ögedei Khan was the parent of Qutuqa Beki, who was in turn succeeded by Genghis Khan. Genghis Khan was the commander at the Battle of Zhongdu, the Battle of the Indus and the Battle of Yehuling. He was the grandfather of Tolui.
London born Geoffrey Chaucer lived in London and died on October 25th, 1400. His occupation was as a bureaucrat. Chaucer was the author of "The Canterbury Tales" and is known for his literary skills and his influence on the likes of Joseph de Maistre. Stuttgart born Georg Wilhelm Friedrich Hegel was born on the 27th of August, 1770 and died in Berlin on 1831-11-14. A Western philosopher and author of the The Phenomenology of Spirit, he also authored the Encyclopedia of the Philosophical Sciences. His work has influenced Predrag Finci, Roberto Mangabeira Unger and Branislav Petronijević.
George Harrison was born in Liverpool in 1943. He was married to Pattie Boyd and later to Olivia Harrison. George's occupation was as a musician and he was known for his songs Be Here Now, Beautiful Girl and Behind That Locked Door. He was a member of The Quarrymen and then The Beatles. He founded Handmade Films and the record label Dark Horse Records. He composed the music for the film Concert for George and Help!. He died in 2001. His son was Dhani Harrison.

George Washington was born in Virginia in the Colony of Virginia and died on Dec. 14, 1799 from epiglottitis. He was married to Martha Washington and his parents were Augustine Washington and Mary Ball Washington. He was a surveyor, planter and was a member of the Independent politician party. He was awarded the Congressional Gold Medal and Thanks of Congress for his service. He founded the Culper Ring and the Commander's Guard and was the founder of Pittsburgh. He was known by Joseph de Maistre, Tobias Lear and Hercules Posey. He was also the first President of the First Bank of the United States. He was succeeded by John Adams and Henry Knox and his tenure was preceded by Joseph de Maistre and Martha Parke Custis and his early life was influenced by Ellen Sharples and Joseph Habersham.

He was a student at the University of Bologna and he founded the CMC Electronics as well as the Marconi Company. The ship Elettra was owned by him.

Henry Ford was born in Springwells Township, Michigan, on July 30, 1863. Ford was married to Clara Jane Bryant and his child was Edsel Ford. Henry Ford was a member of the Democratic Party and the Republican Party in the U.S. Ford was an engineer, businessman, a philanthropist and the designer of the Ford Model C, Ford Model A. and the Ford Model B. (1904). He also designed the Aerocar (1905 automobile) and the Ford Quadricycle. Ford founded Ford Australia, Ford Brasil, and Ford Italia, and he was the owner of USS Truant (PYc-14). Ford died on April 7, 1947. John S. Gray was preceded by Ford as a businessman. Ford is associated with SAE International and the Edison Illuminating Company, and is the key to the organization of SAE International.
Henry II of England was the builder of Hertford Castle, Dover Castle, and The Castle, Newcastle. He started his career in 1154 and finished in 1189. He had several children: Morgan, Eleanor of England, Queen of Castile, Richard I of England, and William, Count of Poitiers (who succeeded Henry II). He married Rosamund Clifford and Eleanor of Aquitaine. He was the predecessor of his own successor, Richard I of England. He also commanded the Battle of Crogen and the Revolt of 1173-1174. His own father was Geoffrey V, Count of Anjou and his mother was Empress Matilda.
Henry VIII of England is the builder of Device Forts and Hertford Castle, and also commanded the battles of Spurs and Rough Wooing. He was also a commander in Bigod's rebellion and founded many institutions such as Christ Church Cathedral School, Christ College, Brecon, the King's (the Cathedral) School, Cambridge University Press, and Elizabeth Wykes, Mark Smeaton, Edward VI, Henry, Duke of Cornwall, Henry FitzRoy, Duke of Richmond and Somerset and Jane Seymour were his spouses. Anne of Cleves was married to him.

Hernando Cortés de Monroy y Pizarro Altamirano (known as Hernán Cortés) was born in Crown of Castile and died in Castilleja de la Cuesta on 1547-12-02. Hernán Cortés was a Conquistador, the founder of Veracruz City and also Mexico City, the father of Leonor Cortés Moctezuma and the grandfather of Martin Cortes (son of Malinche). He was the commander in several key battles, including the Battle of Cempoala, the Battle of Colhuacatan, and the Battle of Otumba. Alonso de Estrada (Tenure 1, 2 and 3), Alonso de Zuazo (Tenure 1) and Cristobal de Tapia (Tenure 1) were all preceded by Hernan Cortes, and Rodrigo de Albornoz (Tenure 3) and Alonso de Estrada (Tenure 2) were all succeeded by him.

James Ephraim Lovelock was born in Letchworth on July 26, 1919 and died on July 26, 2022 in Abbotsbury. He studied earth science and chemistry, and is known for his work on the electron capture detector and the Gaia Hypothesis. He was a mentee of Andy Watson and the author of Novacene and The Revenge of Gaia. Lovelock also influenced Fritjof Capra and Mary Midgley.

Louis Pasteur was born on the 27th of December, 1822 in France and died on the 28th of September, 1895. He was married to Marie Laurent and founded the Alliance Française, the Pasteur Institute and was awarded the Copley Medal, the Rumford Medal, and the Order of the Medjidie. He was a biologist, a mathematician and physicist who was known for his work on Anthrax vaccines, Pasteurization, the germ theory of disease, and was also the one who discovered the microbe responsible for the disease that causes chicken pox. The scientists Émile Roux and Alexandre Yersin were influenced by Pasteur and his work.

Peter Singer, born on July 6, 1946 in Victoria, Australia, is a well known author and philosopher who was influenced by Derek Parfit, John Stuart Mill and Jonathan Glover. He was the founder of the Great Ape Project and starred in the films Lake of Fire, Examined Life and Kangaroo: A Love Hate Story. He wrote Animal Liberation and One World: The Ethics of Globalization and is the author of The Life You Can Save.
Peter Sloterdijk was born in Karlsruhe, 1947-06-26. His writing has been influenced by: Gaston Bachelard, Gilles Deleuze and Friedrich Nietzsche. He writes in the Western philosophy genre. He is the author of Infinite Mobilization, Rage and Time, and Making the Heavens Speak, the latter of which is where Marx Reloaded stars.
Born on July 12, 1920 in Whitehorse, Yukon, Pierre Berton attended the University of British Columbia, before dying on November 30, 2004 in Toronto. Berton wrote books on Canadian history, or Canadiana, which included 1967: The Last Good Year, The Secret World of Og, and Front Page Challenge. He was also a star in the movie, Raoul Wallenberg: Buried Alive. Some of his awards included the Stephen Leacock Memorial Medal for Humour, the Gabrielle Leger award, and The Order of Ontario.
Quebec born Pierre Trudeau (1919-10-18), who died on 28th September 2000, was a lawyer, judge, a member of the Co-operative Commonwealth Federation Party and the Liberal Party of Canada. His spouse was Margaret Trudeau and he had four children: Alexandre, Justin, Michel and Joe. He attended the Universite de Montreal, the College Jean de Brebeuf and Sciences Po. Pierre Trudeau was the commander in the Seven Days to the River Rhine, and was succeeded by Lester B. Pearson, Joe Clark, John Turner, Pierre Trudeau, Kenneth D. Taylor, Roy MacLaren, and Don Jamieson. Margaret Trudeau's spouse was Pierre Trudeau.
The birth name of Pierre de Coubertin was Pierre de Fredy and he was French. He was born in Paris on January 1st 1863 and died in Geneva on the 2nd of September 1937 from a heart attack. His alma mater was the Sciences Po and he was the founder of the International Olympic Committee. He was succeeded by Demetrios Vikelas, Henri de Baillet-Latour, and Sigfrid Edström, and he himself preceded David R. Francis, Tenure 2.
Plato, who was born (0428) in Ancient Greece, where he later died (0348). He was influenced by Pythagoras, Eleusinian Mysteries and Archytas, and known by Manuel Chrysoloras. He wrote the Republic and the Symposium and influenced many others in the Western philosophy region.
Angelo Sodano's predecessor was Pope Benedict XVI who was born in Bavaria on 16 April 1927. His birth name was Joseph Aloisius Ratzinger and his parent was Joseph Ratzinger Sr. Pope Benedict XVI was the author of Jesus of Nazareth: From the Baptism in the Jordan to the Transfiguration, Jesus of Nazareth: The Infancy Narratives and Jesus of Nazareth: Holy Week. He was also succeeded by Pope Francis and his motto is "Cooperators of the truth". He resided in Vatican City.
Ugo Boncompagni (born Bologna, 7 January 1502) became Pope Gregory XIII, who was succeeded by Pope Sixtus V. His alma mater was the University of Bologna. He died in Rome on 10 April 1585. His motto is "Opened and closed". His predecessor was Pope Pius V and his successor was Pope Gregory XIII.
Bruno von Egisheim-Dagsburg, known as Pope Leo IX, was born in the Holy Roman Empire on June 21, 1002. He died in Rome on April 19, 1054. Pope Leo IX's predecessor was Pope Damasus II, and his successor was Pope Victor II. Guardia Lombardi is a place that has had Pope Leo IX as its saint. Pope Leo IX was preceded by Pope Victor II.
Pramoedya Ananta Toer was born in Dutch East Indies on 06-02-1925 and died in Jakarta on 04-03-2006. He was a national of Indonesia and an essayist and novelist, notably the author of the Buru Quartet. Among his other notable works are "This Earth of Mankind", "Footsteps", and "Child of All Nations".
Preston Manning was born in Alberta, on 10th June, 1942. His birth name was Ernest Preston Manning. Manning studied at the University of Alberta and was a member of the Social Credit Party of Canada. He is a resident of Calgary and a member of the Conservative Party of Canada. Bobbie Sparrow's successor was Preston Manning, who was in turn succeeded by Gilles Duceppe and Deborah Grey (Tenure 3). Mr. Manning was also the predecessor to Stephen Harper (Tenure 7). The New Canada was authored by Preston Manning. Mr. Manning is the grandfather of Preston Manning.
The parent of Qin Shi Huang is King Zhuangxiang of Qin who was succeeded by Qin Shi Huang. Qin Shi Huang's parent was Queen Dowager Zhao who had Qin Shi Huang as a child and Fusu was one of Qin Shi Huang's children. Qin Er Shi was a child of Qin Shi Huang and also the successor of Qin Shi Huang. Qin Er Shi preceded Qin Shi Huang. Queen Dowager Zhao's child was Qin Shi Huang. Qin Shi Huang became active in 0221 and was the commander of Qin's Wars of Unification. Qin Shi Huang was succeeded by Qin Er Shi.
Rauf Denktaş was born in British Cyprus, on 27 January 1924 and died in North Nicosia on 13 January 2012. He was a Turkish Cypriot and his child was Serdar Denktaş. He was a member of the National Unity Party in Northern Cyprus. Rauf Denktaş was a vice president under Makarios III and later president under Mehmet Ali Talat, Hakki Atun, Mustafa Cagatay and Nejat Konuk. He was the commander in the invasion of Cyprus. His parent was Rauf Denktaş and his successor was Fazil Küçük.
Born in Descartes, Indre-et-Loire, on the 31st of March, 1596, and died in 1650, in Stockholm, Dutch philosopher René Descartes was influenced by Rodrigo de Arriaga, Jacobus Golius, and Elisabeth of the Palatinate. Descartes wrote the Discourse on the Method, Meditations on First Philosophy, and Principles of Philosophy.
René Lévesque was born in Campbellton, New Brunswick on August 24th, 1922. He died in Quebec on November 1st, 1987 from myocardial infarction. He was a journalist by profession and wrote the book "An Option for Quebec". He served as Prime Minister of Quebec on four separate occasions: under Robert Bourassa, Gilles Lamontagne, Yves Berube and himself.
Eve Branson was the mother of Richard Branson, who is an entrepreneur and the owner of the Virgin Group. Virgin Active was founded by Richard Branson, who was also the founder of Virgin Mobile France and Virgin Australia Holdings. Virgin Records was founded by Branson and is owned by Virgin Group. Branson was also a key person in Fuel (film) and The Culture High. Richard Branson starred in The Superstation.
Richard Burton (birth name: Richard Walter Jenkins Jr) was born in Pontrhydyfen on the 10th of November, 1925 and he died in Celigny on the 5th of August, 1984. He started his career in 1943 and retired in 1984. He was married to Elizabeth Taylor, Sybil Christopher and Sally Burton. He was the father of actress Kate Burton and his career included being a part of the film Candy, the film version of Doctor Faustus, Battle of Sutjeska, and the song Forever Autumn.
Richard Dawkins was born in Nairobi on 1941-03-26 to his parents Lalla and Marian. His birth name is Clinton Richard Dawkins, but he was known for his meme-worthy statements. He studied at the University of Oxford and received his Master of Arts degree and later his Doctor of Philosophy. Richard is also a Fellow of the Royal Society and the author of several books including "An Appetite for Wonder", "The Root of All Evil?", "The Ancestor's Tale", and "Break the Science Barrier". He was also awarded the Zoological Society of London Award, International Cosmos Prize, and the Fellow of the Royal Society award. His key people are Mark Ridley (zoologist) and Richard Dawkins Foundation for Reason and Science, which was founded by him. He was influenced by Christopher Hitchens, W. D. Hamilton and Nikolaas Tinbergen who was his doctoral advisor and he in turn influenced his doctoral student Richard Dawkins. He was also the star of "The Unbelievers" and "The Root of All Evil?".

Born in Petilla de Aragon, Spain, on May 1, 1852, Santiago Ramón y Cajal was a pathologist and histologist with a doctorate in neuroscience. He won the Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine and was known for the discovery of the mossy fiber cell of the hippocampus, interstitial cell of Cajal, and the neuron. He influenced Percival Bailey, Jerome Lettvin, and Jose Manuel Rodriguez Delgado and his student, Blas Cabrera. Ramon y Cajal died in Madrid on October 17, 1934.

Shintaro Ishihara, who died on 1 February 2022 in Japan from pancreatic cancer, was born in the Empire of Japan on 30 September 1932. He was a member of the Liberal Democratic Party in Japan and the Sunrise Party (which he himself led), and was the author of Season of the Sun, Pale Flower and Crazed Fruit. He was the governor of Naoki Inose Tenure 3 and Yukio Aoshima Tenure 1, and Ryutaro Hashimoto Tenure 6 was succeeded by him. He also starred in the movie Samurai Spy. His parents were Yukio Aoshima and Shintaro Ishihara.
Shirin Ebadi was born in Hamadan, Iran, on June 21st, 1947. She attended the University of Tehran. A known defender of Human rights and author of both The Golden Cage and Iran Awakening, she was the recipient of the Interfaith Centre of New York award, the Nobel Peace Prize and also, the Legion of Honour.
Sigismund Schlomo Freud, known as Sigmund Freud, was born on the 6th May 1856 in the Austrian Empire. He was married to Martha Bernays and had two children called Ernst L Freud and Anna Freud. He studied neurology and psychoanalysis at the University of Vienna and later influenced by Schopenhauer and Josef Breuer. He also knew Empedocles. He was known for psychoanalysis, the Oedipus complex, Repression (psychology), On Narcissism, Beyond the pleasure principle and Introduction to Psychoanalysis. German Empire-born Werner Heisenberg, who died on 01/02/1976 in Bavaria, was awarded the Matteucci Medal, the Barnard Medal for Meritorious Service to Science, and the Pour le Mérite for Sciences and Arts. His birth date is 12/05/1901. He studied Theoretical Physics at the University of Gottingen and the University of Munich. Doctoral students of Werner Heisenberg included Arnold Sommerfeld, Edward Teller, Friedwardt Winterberg, and Rudolf Schulten. His alma mater was the University of Gottingen. He was the doctoral advisor of Reinhard Oehme and the author of The Physical Principles of the Quantum Theory. Jochen Heisenberg and Martin Heisenberg were his children. He is known for the canonical commutation relation, Quantum fluctuation, and Quantum field theory. His awards include the Barnard Medal for Meritorious Service to Science, the Pour le Mérite for Sciences and Arts, and the Matteucci Medal.
